And its cause: the emission of semen that has gushing and lust. [1] His saying: 'and its cause' – with kasra on jim – meaning what makes ghusl obligatory. It would have been more appropriate by analogy to what he mentioned in the section on wudu and its nullifiers, although they share the same characteristic, because every hadath nullifies what came before and necessitates what comes after. [2] His saying: 'emission' – is a verbal noun from nazala with damma on nun, which is the fluid of a man. It is said: a man emitted (anzala), he became one having nazala. The intended meaning here is exit, by virtue of its addition to semen, as stated by al-Birjandi. And exiting to outside the body or what is in its ruling like the external private part and the foreskin is conditional, according to one view. As long as it is in the urethra or internal vagina, ghusl is not obligatory. He said in 'al-Ghunya'. [3] His saying: 'semen' – with fatha on meem and kasra on noon and tashdid on the last letter – and it is general, including the fluid of a man and the fluid of a woman. It has characteristics by which it is known: one of them: exiting with lust followed by weakness. Second: the smell like the smell of pollen. Third: exiting with gushing and spurts. All this is about the semen of a man. As for the semen of a woman, it is thin and yellow, as stated by al-Nawawi. As for madhi: it is the thin fluid that exits upon weak lust through play and the like without gushing. So it obligates wudu, not ghusl. And wadi: it is a thick white fluid with no smell, exiting after urine. So it obligates wudu, not ghusl. [4] His saying: 'having gushing' – with fatha – i.e., flowing quickly and pouring strongly, and it is a description at the time of separation, such that if he emits without lust, ghusl is not obligatory according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. It is found in both the male and female semen as chosen in 'Ghayah al-Bayan', 'Jami' al-Rumuz', 'Ma'alim al-Tanzil', and others. And some deny gushing in the semen of a woman, but it is not correct as I have expanded in 'al-Si'ayah'. If you say: mentioning both gushing and lust is only correct according to the statement of Abu Yusuf because he stipulates gushing and lust at the time of exit, not according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), for they did not stipulate gushing at the time of exit; rather they said ghusl becomes obligatory when the semen leaves its place with lust, then the lust subsides and it exits without gushing. I say: It is correct according to all, because if semen exits with lust and gushing, ghusl is obligatory according to all. The only case according to them is the case of semen exiting with lust at separation without gushing, and there is no difficulty in it. [1] His saying: 'at the time of separation' – i.e., its separation from its place and resting point, which is the backbone in men and the collarbone (i.e., bones of the chest) in women. This is connected to the condition of lust, not to gushing, for it only occurs at the time of exit. [2] His saying: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – for he says that ghusl is obligatory from the emission of semen.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn defining the cause of ghusl (obligatory bath) in the Hanafi school. It opens by explaining the term 'موجبه' as what makes ghusl obligatory. The cause is emission of semen (إنزال مَنِي) with two conditions: that it exits with gushing flow (دفق) and with lust (شهوة). The commentary then defines each term. It stresses that the exit must be to the outside of the body; if semen remains inside the urethra or vagina, ghusl is not required. The properties of male semen are described: exit with lust followed by relaxation, a pollen-like smell, and gushing spurts. Female semen is thin and yellow. Then two other fluids are distinguished: madhi (pre-ejaculatory fluid) and wadi (post-urine discharge), both only require wudu, not ghusl. The key issue is the condition of lust: if semen exits without lust, ghusl is not obligatory according to the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who requires ghusl from any emission of semen. The commentary then addresses an internal Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf requires gushing as well, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not; they deem lust sufficient at the moment of separation from its resting place, even if the gushing occurs after lust subsides. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that lust is the essential condition, and gushing is not required, though the matn included it to cover the full cause according to Abu Yusuf. Finally, the passage explains that 'عند الانفصال' refers to separation from the backbone (for men) or collarbone (for women), and it is connected to lust, not gushing.

Key Terms
مَنِي (maniy): Semen, includes male and female, characterized by exit with lust, strong smell, and gushing flow.
د فق (dafaq): Gushing, flowing quickly and strongly, a description of semen at the time of separation.
شهوة (shahwah): Lust, sexual desire, a necessary condition for ghusl according to Hanafis.
انفصال (infisal): Separation of semen from its place (backbone/collarbone), must occur while lust is present.
مذي (madhy): Pre-ejaculatory fluid, thin, exits with weak desire, obligates only wudu.
ودي (wady): Post-urine discharge, thick, white, no smell, obligates only wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Conditions for Wajib Ghusl: Shahwa and Dafq - Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions for obligatory ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether shahwa and dafq are required for ghusl, state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only if semen exits with shahwa; the dispute is whether shahwa must be at separation or exit.

This passage from Umdat al-Riayah presents a critical intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the conditions that make ghusl obligatory. While all Hanafi imams agree that mere emission without desire does not necessitate ghusl, they differ on the role of shahwa (sexual desire) and dafq (gushing) at two stages: separation (insifal) and exit (khuruj). Understanding this distinction has direct implications for when a Muslim must perform ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify common ground and point of dispute
All Hanafi imams agree that ghusl is wajib only when semen exits, not merely upon separation from its reservoir. They also agree that shahwa is required at separation. The dispute is whether shahwa (and dafq) must be present at exit as well.
The Shafi'i view (any emission requires ghusl) is rejected by all Hanafis.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: shahwa is required only at separation (insifal). Abu Yusuf: shahwa and dafq (gushing) must be present at exit (khuruj).
Dafq only occurs at exit, so it cannot be required at separation.
3
Examine the proofs
The Hanafi proof for requiring shahwa is the hadith 'Idha fadakht al-ma' faghtasil' (When you eject water, perform ghusl) – ejection (fadkh) implies shahwa and dafq. The opposing proof is the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma' (water from water) which was reported as a concession and later abrogated.
The abrogation of 'al-ma' min al-ma' is key to the Hanafi argument.
4
Analyse the thamarah (practical differences)
If semen separates with shahwa but desire subsides before exit (no dafq), ghusl is wajib according to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad but not according to Abu Yusuf. Similarly, residual semen after incomplete ghusl requires a second ghusl in their view but not in Abu Yusuf's.
These scenarios highlight the real-life impact of the ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih reasoning
Later Hanafi works (al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Nawazil) adopt Abu Yusuf's view as the operative position for fatwa. Ghayat al-Bayan explains that Abu Yusuf's view is qiyas, while Abu Hanifa's is istihsan for caution.
The tarjih is based on the method of qiyas being preferred to istihsan in this issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة/ الغسل
عند الانفصال
٣٥٧
عند الانفصال حتى لو أنزل بلا شهوة لا يجب الغسلُ عندنا ، خلافاً للشافعي"
يوجد في مني الرجل والمرأة كليهما كما اختاره في «غاية البيان»، و«جامع الرموز، و «معالم التنزيل»، وغيرها. ومنهم من أنكر الدفق في مَنِي ،المرأة، وليس بصحيح كما بسطته في «السعاية». فإن قلت : ذكر الدفق والشهوة كليهما إنّما يستقيم على قول أبي يوسف له لاشتراطه الدفق والشهوة عند الخروج لا على قولهما ، فإنهما لم يشترطا الدفق عند بوجوبِ الغُسلِ إذا زالَ المَنِي عن مكانه بشهوة، ثم سكنت الشهوة
الخروج حتى قالا
وخرج من غير دفق.
قلت: هو مستقيم على قول الكلّ ، فإنه إذا خرج المني بشهوة ودفق يجبُ الغُسِلُ عند الكل، غاية الأمر بعض الموجبات على رأيهما، وهو خروج المني بشهوة عند

Book of Taharah / Ghusl
Upon separation
357
Upon separation: Even if one emits without desire, ghusl is not obligatory according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i.
It exists in the semen of both man and woman as chosen in 'Ghayat al-Bayan', 'Jami' al-Rumuz', 'Ma'alim al-Tanzil', and others. And some denied the gushing in the semen of woman, and it is not correct as I have detailed in 'al-Sa'ayah'. If you say: Mentioning both gushing and desire is only consistent with the statement of Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – because he stipulates gushing and desire at the time of exit, not with their statement, for they did not stipulate gushing at exit; rather they said: If the semen moves from its place with desire, then desire subsides, and it exits without gushing, ghusl becomes obligatory.
I say: It is consistent with the statement of all, for when semen exits with desire and gushing, ghusl is obligatory according to all. The only difference is that according to their view, some causes are the exit of semen with desire at the time of separation without gushing, and there is no difficulty in that. [1] His saying: 'upon separation' means its separation from its place and its resting place, which is the spine in man, and the chest bones in woman, and this is connected to the condition of desire, not to gushing, for gushing only occurs at exit. [2] His saying: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – for he says that ghusl is obligatory from the exit of semen.
(3)
And al-Babarti pointed this out in 'al-'Inayah 'ala al-Hidayah' (1:53), and the author of 'Majma' al-Anhur' (1:23), and al-Haskafi in 'al-Durr al-Muntaqa' (1:23), and 'Radd al-Muhtar' (1:109), and others. Although he [the matn author] restricted it as restricted by the author of al-Hidayah (1:17), and 'al-Ikhtiyar' (1:20), and 'al-Kanz' (p.), and 'al-Multaqa' (p.4), and al-Quduri in his 'Mukhtasar' (p.3).
(1) 'Jami' al-Rumuz sharh al-Nuqayah' (1:26).
(2) 'al-Sa'ayah' (1:309).
(3) See: 'Mughni al-Muhtaj' (1:70) and 'Sharh al-Shihab al-Ramli 'ala al-Sittin Mas'alah' by al-Dimyati (p.44), and 'Hashiya Ahmad al-Mahi' (p.24).
(His marginalia)
358
'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah
Then, desire is a condition at the time of separation according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and at the time of exit according to Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – such that if it separates from its place with desire, and the tip of the organ is taken until his desire subsides, then it exits without desire, ghusl is obligatory according to them (the two), not according to him (Abu Yusuf). And if he performed ghusl before urinating, then some of the semen remains and exits, a second ghusl becomes obligatory according to them, not according to him. Absolutely, even if without desire, due to the generality of the hadith 'Water is from water' meaning ghusl is obligatory from the exit of semen, reported by Muslim, Ahmad, al-Bazzar, and others.
(1)
And for us: the hadith: 'When you eject water, then perform ghusl' reported by Abu Dawud, and in the narration of Ahmad: 'When you throw water, then perform ghusl', and throwing and ejecting only occurs with gushing and desire. Thus said al-'Ayni. And in this topic there are discussions mentioned in 'al-Sa'ayah' (4).
[1] His saying: 'Then desire...' – Know that after they agreed that ghusl is obligatory only upon the exit of semen from the penis, not merely its separation from its place, they differed as to whether the conjunction of desire with exit is required. According to Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – it is required, because the obligation of ghusl is dependent on both separation and exit, and desire is required at separation by consensus, so likewise at exit. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is not, because when desire is found at separation, the name of janabah (major impurity) is found, so ghusl becomes obligatory without stipulating an additional condition. And it is said in 'al-Tatarkhaniyyah' quoting from 'al-Nawazil': 'We adopt the statement of Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him.' End. And in 'Ghayat al-Bayan': 'The statement of Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – is qiyas (analogy), and the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is istihsan (juristic preference) out of caution in matters of worship.'
(0)
[2] His saying: 'such that...' is an explanation of the practical consequence of the difference between them and Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him.
:
(1) In Sahih Muslim (1:269), Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1:188), al-Mujtaba (1:115), Musnad Ahmad (18:125, and others, but from Ubayy ibn Ka'b – may Allah be pleased with him – who said: 'Water is from water was a concession in early Islam, then it was abrogated' reported in Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1:183), Sunan Abi Dawud (1:105), Sahih Ibn Hibban (3:448), and others.
(2) In Sunan Abi Dawud (1:102), Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (1:108), Musnad Ahmad (1:109), Sahih Ibn Hibban (3:391), and others.
(3) In 'al-Binayah' (1:267), and in it also: al-khadhf and al-fadgh is the gushing.
(4) 'al-Sa'ayah' (1:311).
(5) From 'al-Fatawa al-Tatarkhaniyyah' (1:118).
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions that make ghusl obligatory. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: if one emits semen without sexual desire, ghusl is not obligatory, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who holds that any emission of semen requires ghusl regardless of desire. The discussion then focuses on the necessity of two conditions: shahwa (sexual desire) and dafq (gushing flow) at the time of separation (insifal) and exit (khuruj). The text clarifies that dafq only occurs at exit, while shahwa can be present at separation. The main intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) on one side, and Abu Yusuf on the other. Abu Yusuf stipulates that shahwa must be present at the moment of exit for ghusl to be wajib; he also requires dafq. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad only require shahwa at the time of separation (when the semen leaves its reservoir) and do not require it at exit. They consider the name janabah established when shahwa is present at separation. The text then presents a thamarah (practical consequence): if the semen separates from its place with desire but then the desire subsides and it exits without desire, ghusl is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad but not according to Abu Yusuf. Similarly, if one performs ghusl before urinating and then residual semen exits, a second ghusl is wajib in their view, but not in Abu Yusuf's view. The proof cited by Abu Yusuf and the Shafi'is is the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma' (water from water), which the text notes was a concession later abrogated. The Hanafi argument for requiring desire is the hadith from Abu Dawud: 'Idha fadakht al-ma' faghtasil' (When you eject water, perform ghusl), where 'ejecting' (fadkh/khadhf) implies dafq and shahwa. The commentary by the author explains that the term 'shahwa' in the original text is connected with 'insifal' (separation) not 'khuruj' (exit). Finally, the author notes that in al-Tatarkhaniyyah and al-Nawazil, the mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Yusuf, while in Ghayat al-Bayan, Abu Yusuf's view is described as qiyas and the others' as istihsan for caution in worship.

Key Terms
شهوة (shahwa): Sexual desire or arousal, a condition for the obligation of ghusl when separating semen from its place (at insifal) or at exit (khuruj), depending on the imam.
دفق (dafq): The gushing or forceful ejection of semen, which only occurs at exit, not at separation.
انفصال (insifal): Separation of semen from its place (spine for men, chest for women); its occurrence with shahwa is the basis for janabah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
خروج (khuruj): Exit of semen from the body; according to Abu Yusuf, shahwa at this point is required for ghusl to be wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position mentioned in this passage, when does ghusl become obligatory?
A) When semen separates from its place with shahwa, regardless of exit conditions
B) When semen exits with both shahwa and dafq, as per Abu Yusuf's view
C) When any semen is emitted, even without desire
D) Only when semen exits but without any condition

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires both shahwa (desire) and dafq (gushing) at the moment of exit for ghusl to be obligatory.

Timing of Arousal for Ghusl: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of shahwa for ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the condition of shahwa for ghusl and explain the practical consequence of this intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
Ghusl requires semen exit with arousal, but the timing of the arousal condition is disputed: at detachment or at exit.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on a specific condition for ghusl: whether sexual arousal (shahwa) must be present at the moment semen exits the body or only at its initial detachment from the source. While all three imams agree that ghusl is obligatory only upon exit, not mere detachment, they differ on the timing of the arousal condition. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly determining when ghusl becomes wajib in borderline cases, such as when arousal subsides before semen fully exits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed foundation
All Hanafi imams agree that ghusl becomes wajib only upon the exit (khuruj) of semen from the penis, not upon its detachment (infisal) from the testicles. Establish this baseline before examining the dispute.
This agreement rules out the possibility that ghusl is required upon detachment alone.
2
State the two positions on shahwa
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that arousal must be present at the time of detachment from the source. Abu Yusuf holds that arousal must be present at the time of exit from the penis. Identify each position clearly.
Both positions stem from different understandings of the relevant hadiths.
3
Work through the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply the positions to a case: semen detaches with arousal, then the person holds the penis until arousal ceases, and then it exits without arousal. According to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, ghusl is wajib because arousal was present at detachment. According to Abu Yusuf, ghusl is not wajib because arousal was absent at exit.
This is the key difference that affects daily practice.
4
Understand the tarjih and its basis
Learn that later Hanafi authorities (al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Nawazil, Ghayat al-Bayan) adopt Abu Yusuf's view as the mufta bihi. His position is described as qiyas (analogy), while Abu Hanifa's is istihsan (precaution). The tarjih weighs qiyas as stronger in this case.
The mufta bihi ruling is that ghusl is not wajib if arousal is absent at exit.

Source Text

(1) ولنا : حديث : «إذا فضحت الماء فاغتسل (۳) أخرجه أبو داود، وفي رواية أحمد : «إذا خذفت الماء فاغتسل»، والخذف والفضح لا يكون إلا مع الدفق والشهوة، كذا قال العيني)، وفي المقام مباحث مذكورة في «السعاية»(4). [۱] قوله : ثم الشهوة ... الخ ؛ اعلم أنهم بعد اتفاقهم على أن الغُسل لا يجب إلا بخروج المني من الذكر لا بمجرد انفصاله من مقره، اختلفوا في أنه هل تشترط مقارنةً الشهوة للخروج، فعند أبي يوسف الله يشترط ؛ لأنَّ وجوبَ الغُسلِ منوط بالانفصال والخروج كليهما، وقد شُرطت الشهوة عند الانفصال اتفاقاً، فكذا عند الخروج أيضاً. وعندهما لا ؛ لأنه إذا وجدت الشهوة عند الانفصال وجد اسم الجنابة، فيجب الغُسلُ من غير اشتراط أمر زائد وقال في «التاتارخانية» نقلاً عن «النوازل»: «بقول أبي ، يوسف له نأخذ». انتهى) . وفي غاية البيان»: «قول أبي يوسف له هو القياس ، وقول أبي حنيفة ومحمد ه استحسان للاحتياط في أمر العبادة». [٢]قوله : حتى ...الخ ؛ بيان لثمرة الخلاف بينهما وبين أبي يوسف الله.
Then, sexual arousal is a condition at the time of detachment according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and at the time of exit according to Abu Yusuf. So if [the semen] detached with arousal from its place, and he grasped the head of the penis until his arousal subsided, and it exited without arousal, ghusl is obligatory according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), not according to him (Abu Yusuf). And if he performed ghusl before urinating, then a remainder of semen exited from him, a second ghusl is obligatory according to the two, not according to him, absolutely, even if without arousal; due to the general application of the hadith 'Water is from water,' i.e., ghusl is obligatory from the exit of semen. It was narrated by Muslim, Ahmad, al-Bazzar and others. And for us: the hadith 'When you emit water with force, then perform ghusl' narrated by Abu Dawud, and in Ahmad's narration: 'When you expel water with force, then perform ghusl.' And expulsion and emission with force only occur with gush and arousal, as al-'Ayni said. And in this subject there are discussions mentioned in al-Si'aya. [1] His statement: 'Then arousal...' etc.; know that after they agreed that ghusl is only obligatory by the exit of semen from the penis, not merely by its detachment from its reservoir, they differed on whether the concomitance of arousal with exit is required. According to Abu Yusuf, it is required, because the obligation of ghusl is dependent on both detachment and exit, and arousal at detachment is agreed upon as a condition, so likewise at exit. According to the two, it is not required, because when arousal is found at detachment, the term janabah is established, so ghusl becomes obligatory without requiring an additional matter. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya, quoting from al-Nawazil: 'We adopt the statement of Abu Yusuf.' End. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'The statement of Abu Yusuf is qiyas, and the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is istihsan for precaution in matters of worship.' [2] His statement: 'So that...' etc.; an explanation of the practical consequence of the difference between them and Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether sexual arousal (shahwa) must be present at the moment semen exits the body for ghusl to become obligatory. The author first states the positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require arousal at the time the semen detaches from its source (the testicles), while Abu Yusuf requires it at the time it exits the penis. The practical difference is illustrated: if semen detaches with arousal, then the person holds the head of the penis until arousal subsides, and then it exits without arousal, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, ghusl is wajib because arousal was present at detachment. According to Abu Yusuf, ghusl is not wajib because arousal was absent at exit. Similarly, if one performs ghusl before urinating, and then a residual amount of semen exits (even without arousal), a second ghusl is wajib according to the two, but not according to Abu Yusuf. The proof for Abu Yusuf and the opposing school (Shafi'i) is the general hadith 'Water is from water' meaning ghusl is required from any emission of semen. The Hanafi response cites the hadith 'When you emit water with force, then perform ghusl' which implies gush and arousal, thus limiting the obligation. The commentary explains that Abu Yusuf's opinion is qiyas (analogy) because he considers both detachment and exit, requiring arousal at both. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's opinion is istihsan (juristic preference) out of caution in worship. However, the later preferred position for fatwa, as per al-Tatarkhaniyya, is the opinion of Abu Yusuf. The authority weight of the main ruling from the matn is from Zahir al-Riwayah, but the tarjih leans towards Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
الشهوة (al-shahwa): Sexual arousal; the physical sensation accompanying ejaculation.
الانفصال (al-infisal): Detachment of semen from its source (the testicles) within the body.
الخروج (al-khuruj): Exit of semen from the penis to the outside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if semen detaches with arousal, then exits without arousal, what is the ruling?
A) Ghusl is obligatory.
B) Ghusl is not obligatory.
C) Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory.
D) Ghusl is obligatory only if he urinates first.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is wajib upon semen exit; the condition of arousal at detachment suffices for Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf requires arousal at exit, and this is the preferred fatwa.

Ghusl After Nocturnal Emission: Wetness Requirement and Women's Ruling
Rulings on ghusl after ihtilam and equality of women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for ghusl after ihtilam and explain why women follow the same ruling as men, using the hadith of Umm Sulaym.

Core Idea
Ghusl after a wet dream is only wajib if wetness is found — memory without wetness is not enough for both men and women.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the ruling for ghusl after nocturnal emission, clarifying scenarios based on the presence or absence of wetness. He affirms that men and women are treated equally: the decisive factor is seeing wetness, not merely remembering the dream. This is supported by a well-known hadith and a rejection of a weak narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for ihtilam
The commentary states: even if emission occurs during sleep, the ruling is the same. Ghusl is only required if wetness is seen.
This is the established Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Recognize the three scenarios
Three possibilities after waking: (1) remembers dream and sees wetness → ghusl; (2) remembers dream but no wetness → no ghusl; (3) no memory but sees wetness → ghusl.
3
Confirm women's equivalence
Women follow the same rule: if she sees wetness, ghusl is wajib; if not, no ghusl, regardless of memory. Proof: hadith of Umm Sulaym.
The hadith states: 'Yes, if she sees water.'
4
Evaluate the weak narration
A weak narration from Muhammad says a woman must perform ghusl if she remembers dream, emission, and pleasure, even without wetness. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani rejects it as not acted upon.
This narration is from Nawadir, not Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Analyze the author's critique
The author of al-Hidayah accepted the weak narration in some works, justifying it by claiming a woman's fluid does not gush. The commentator denies this, stating that lack of gush is not proven.
The critique reinforces the majority view.

(And even if in sleep, and there is no difference in this between the man and the woman. And it is narrated from Muhammad in non-reliable transmissions: If a woman remembers the dream, emission, and pleasure, and does not see wetness, ghusl is upon her. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: This transmission is not to be acted upon. [1] His statement: 'And even if in sleep' – i.e., even if the emission of semen occurs during sleep. If he wakes up and remembers the dream and does not see wetness on his body or his bed, no ghusl upon him. If he remembers the dream and sees wetness, or does not remember and sees wetness, ghusl is obligatory upon him; due to the hadith 'Water is from water' as mentioned. [2] His statement: 'Between the man and the woman' – for if she sees wetness, ghusl is obligatory upon her, whether she remembers the semen or not; due to the hadith of Umm Sulaym that she asked the Messenger of Allah about it, and he answered that ghusl is obligatory upon her when she sees water. It was narrated by al-Tirmidhi, Muslim, al-Bukhari and others. And on this subject there are traditions that we have expanded in al-Si'aya. [3] His statement: 'Ghusl is upon her' – this is what the author of al-Hidayah chose in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil and in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid. Its justification is that her (woman's) fluid does not stand like a man's fluid; rather it descends from her chest. And what is in it is not hidden: Firstly, the absence of gush in it is denied.)
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings of ghusl after nocturnal emission (ihtilam). The author first states the general rule: even if the emission occurs during sleep, the ruling is the same. He then explains the scenarios: (1) If a person wakes up and remembers a wet dream but sees no wetness on his body or bed, no ghusl is required. (2) If he remembers the dream and sees wetness, or does not remember but sees wetness, ghusl is wajib. The proof is the hadith 'Water is from water' – meaning ghusl is obligatory from the exit of seminal fluid. The author then confirms that women have the same ruling as men: if a woman sees wetness, ghusl is wajib, whether she remembers the dream or not. This is based on the hadith of Umm Sulaym where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Yes, if she sees water.' The author mentions that there is a weak narration from Muhammad (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) stating that if a woman remembers the dream, emission, and pleasure, but does not see wetness, ghusl is still required. However, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani rejects this narration as not to be acted upon. The author then notes that the author of al-Hidayah accepted this weak ruling in some of his later works, justifying it by the fact that a woman's fluid does not 'stand' like a man's but descends from her chest. The commentator of the present work (probably the author of 'Umda al-Ri'aya) criticizes this justification, first by denying that there is no gush in a woman's emission. The overall authority weight: the primary ruling (from the matn) is Zahir al-Riwayah, while the narration from Muhammad is from Nawadir and not adopted.

Key Terms
احتلام (ihtilam): A wet dream; nocturnal emission of semen.
بلل (balal): Wetness; the physical sign of semen on clothes or body.
غسل (ghusl): Full-body ritual washing required for janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ghusl is wajib because she remembers.
B) Ghusl is wajib only if she sees wetness.
C) Ghusl is sunnah.
D) She must perform wudu only.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl after a nocturnal emission is obligatory only upon seeing wetness, regardless of memory, and this applies equally to men and women.

Ghusl Upon Finding Wetness After Sleep: Ruling and Dispute
Explains ruling of ghusl for wetness after sleep with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after finding wetness upon waking, distinguish the conditions for men and women, and evaluate the rejected narration regarding women's ghusl.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only upon certain knowledge of emission—recollection of a wet dream alone is insufficient.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the ruling on ghusl after sleep. It clarifies that finding wetness (semen) triggers ghusl regardless of dream recollection, while the absence of wetness with only recollection does not. The passage also addresses a specific dispute about women, where a minority narration is rejected based on authentic hadith and usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for men
Determine when ghusl is wajib for a man after sleep based on the text: if he finds wetness (balal) or has certainty of emission, regardless of dream recollection.
The hadith 'al-ma'u min al-ma'' is cited.
2
Identify the ruling for women
For women, the same principle applies: ghusl is wajib upon finding wetness or certainty of emission, as per the hadith of Umm Sulaym.
The text emphasizes 'if she sees water'.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Analyze the two main hadith: the general 'water from water' and the specific response to Umm Sulaym. Understand that they condition ghusl on the presence of water.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni in transmission and indication.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
A narration from Imam Muhammad says if a woman remembers a wet dream and pleasure but finds no wetness, ghusl is still wajib. The author rejects this, arguing it contradicts the hadith and female semen does gush.
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and others choose non-obligation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that ghusl is not wajib unless the woman knows (by sight or certainty) that fluid exited. This is based on the authentic hadith and rejection of the weak narration.
The tarjih authority is Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani.

Book of Purity/ Ghusl. 'And even if in sleep.' [1] His statement: 'and even if in sleep'; meaning even if semen exits during sleep, then when he wakes up, if he recollects the wet dream and does not see wetness on his body or his bedding, there is no ghusl upon him. And if he recollects the wet dream and sees wetness, or does not recollect and sees it, ghusl is obligatory upon him due to the hadith: 'Water is from water' as mentioned before. [11] His statement: 'Between man and woman', for indeed if she sees wetness, ghusl is obligatory upon her, whether she recollects the semen or not; due to the hadith of Umm Sulaym that she asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ about it, and he answered that ghusl is obligatory upon her if she sees water. This was recorded by al-Tirmidhi, Muslim, al-Bukhari, and others. And in this chapter there are ahadith that we have detailed in 'al-Si'aya'. [3] His statement: 'Ghusl is obligatory upon her'; this is what the author of al-Hidayah chose in 'Mukhtarat al-Nawazil' and in 'al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd'. His reasoning is that her water (semen) is not stationary like a man's water, but rather descends from her chest. And it is not hidden what is in it: Firstly, the lack of gushing is denied. (1) Its wording: From Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her) she said: Umm Sulaym came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: O Messenger of Allah, Allah is not shy of the truth, is there ghusl upon a woman if she has a wet dream? The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Yes, if she sees water.' (Sahih Muslim, Sahih al-Bukhari, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, etc.) (2) And from them, from A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) she said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ was asked about a man who finds wetness but does not remember a wet dream. He said: He performs ghusl. And about a man who thinks he had a wet dream but does not find wetness. He said: There is no ghusl upon him. Umm Salamah said: O Messenger of Allah, is there ghusl upon a woman if she sees that? He said: Yes, indeed women are the counterparts of men. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, al-Sunan al-Sughra, al-Muntaqa, Sunan Abi Dawud, Musnad Ahmad, etc.) (3) al-Si'aya (1:314). (4) al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd (1:177). Secondly, because the ahadith tied the obligation of ghusl upon her to seeing water, and the intent is obtaining knowledge of its exit, whether by sight or otherwise. So if she does not know of its exit, what is the basis for obligating ghusl? Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani chose non-obligation and rejected the narration of obligation, as did the author of al-Khulasa and others.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on ghusl due to seminal discharge after sleep, with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding women. The commentary begins by explaining the base text: if a person wakes up and finds wetness, ghusl is obligatory regardless of whether they recall a wet dream; if they recall a wet dream but find no wetness, no ghusl is required. This is based on the hadith 'al-ma'u min al-ma'' (water from water), meaning ghusl is only required when water (semen) is emitted. The author then addresses the ruling for women: if a woman finds wetness, ghusl is obligatory, citing the hadith of Umm Sulaym where the Prophet ﷺ said 'yes, if she sees water.' A minority narration attributed to Imam Muhammad states that if a woman remembers a wet dream and pleasure but finds no wetness, ghusl is still obligatory, arguing that female semen does not gush like male semen and may not be visible. This narration is rejected by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, who argues that the ahadith clearly tie obligation to seeing (or knowing of) the water, so without knowledge there is no obligation. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that ghusl is only obligatory when the woman knows that fluid has exited, whether by sight or other means. The passage thus clarifies that the Hanafi school does not require ghusl for women who experience arousal without detectable emission, contrary to the weak narration.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniyy): Semen or female ejaculate; its emission (whether by sight or certainty) necessitates ghusl.
الاحتلام (al-ihtilām): Wet dream; sexual dream that may or may not result in emission.
البلل (al-balal): Wetness; refers to semen or discharge found after sleep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whenever she remembers a wet dream, regardless of wetness.
B) Only if she sees or is certain that fluid exited.
C) Only if she experienced pleasure during the dream.
D) Whenever she finds wetness or remembers a dream with pleasure.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl after sleep is only wajib upon knowledge of emission, not mere dream recollection; the minority view for women is rejected.

Ghusl Obligation upon Penetration: The Rule of Ghaybat al-Hashafah
Commentary explaining the ruling of ghusl obligation upon penetration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl due to intercourse and apply the hadith proof to distinguish between penetration and mere emission.

Core Idea
Ghusl becomes obligatory upon insertion of the glans into the vagina or anus, whether or not semen is emitted.

This lesson examines a foundational taharah ruling: the moment ghusl becomes wajib due to sexual intercourse. The commentator defines key anatomical terms and anchors the ruling in a clear hadith, while also noting an important exception when penetration does not occur. Understanding this distinction is essential for both personal practice and teaching others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act triggers ghusl? The disappearance (ghaybat) of the glans (hashafah) into the vagina or anus. The ruling is that ghusl becomes wajib for both parties upon this act.
The term 'ghaybat al-hashafah' is the legal threshold.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he emits or not.' This is the primary evidence for the ruling.
The hadith is recorded by al-Tabarani and found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the condition
The cause (sabab) is the disappearance of the glans, not the emission of semen. The hadith explicitly negates the requirement of emission with 'whether he emits or not.'
This removes any confusion that ghusl is only for janabah due to ejaculation.
4
Note the exception
If the glans does not disappear (e.g., intercourse between thighs) and semen flows into the vagina, ghusl is not obligatory on the woman because the obligating cause did not occur. The man would still need ghusl due to emission.
This exception is from al-Khulasa.
5
Confirm the ruling applies to both parties
The commentary clarifies that the ruling is for both the active and passive participants (al-fa'il and al-maf'ul bihi).
Ghusl becomes wajib on both even if only one party inserted the glans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وغيبة ... الخ ؛ الغَيبة - بالفتح – مصدر غاب الشيء إذا استتر والحشفة بفتحات رأس الذكر إلى المقطع والقبل : بالضم وسكون الباء وبضمتين : فرج المرأة. والدبر : بالضم وبضمتين. وفيه إشارة إلى أن موجب الغسل نفس الإدخال، وإن لم ينزل الحديث : «إذا التقى الختانان وغابت الحشفة، وجب الغسل أنزلَ أو لم ينزل»)، أخرجه الطبراني وغيره ونحوه في «صحيح البخاري» و«مسلم» والسنن وغيرها(۳). وإلى أنه لو جامع فيما دون الفرج ولم تغب الحشفة إلا أنه خرج المني وسالَ إلى الفرج لا يجب عليها الغُسل كما في «الخلاصة».
His statement: 'and disappearance... etc.'; al-ghaybah (with fatha) is the masdar of ghāba 'l-shay'u 'when something becomes hidden'; al-hashafah (with three fatha movements) is the head of the penis up to the circumcision cut; al-qabul (with damm and sukun on ba' or with two dammas) is the vagina of a woman; al-dubur (with damm or two dammas) is the anus. It contains an indication that the cause of ghusl is the insertion itself, even if no semen is emitted, due to the hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he emits or not.' Recorded by al-Tabarani and others, and similar in Sahih al-Bukhari, Muslim, and Sunan, etc. (3). And that if one has intercourse below the private part and the glans does not disappear, but semen exits and flows to the private part, ghusl is not obligatory upon her, as in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn stating 'and disappearance of the glans in the front or back, upon the doer and the one done to.' It defines key terms: al-ghaybah (disappearance), al-hashafah (glans of the penis), al-qabul (vagina), al-dubur (anus). The main ruling is that the obligating cause (mujib) of ghusl is the very act of insertion (idkhal) of the glans into the vagina or anus, whether or not semen is emitted. The proof is the hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he emits or not.' The hadith is quoted from al-Tabarani and also found in Bukhari and Muslim with similar wording. The passage also notes an exception: if intercourse occurs outside the private parts (e.g., between thighs) and the glans does not disappear, but semen exits and flows into the vagina, ghusl is not obligatory upon the woman because the obligating cause (ghaybat al-hashafah) did not occur. The ghusl would be wajib upon the man due to emission, but the woman does not need ghusl because there was no penetration and no emission from her. This nuance is from al-Khulasa. The ruling applies to both parties (al-fa'il and al-maf'ul bihi) equally when penetration occurs.

Key Terms
غيبة الحشفة (ghaybat al-hashafah): The disappearance of the glans of the penis into the vagina or anus; this is the minimum threshold for ghusl obligation due to intercourse.
الحشفة (al-hashafah): The glans of the penis, from its tip to the circumcision cut (al-maqta').
القبل (al-qabul): The vagina of a woman; also referred to as farj.
الدبر (al-dubur): The anus; penetration here also necessitates ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only when semen is emitted.
B) When the glans disappears into the vagina or anus, regardless of emission.
C) Only if both parties experience orgasm.
D) When the two bodies touch without penetration.

Key Takeaway
The cause of ghusl is the disappearance of the glans during intercourse; emission is irrelevant.

Ghusl Due to Disappearance of the Glans (Ghaybat al-Hashafah)
States ruling and prophetic proof for ghusl due to insertion of glans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sole condition that triggers the obligation of ghusl from intercourse and explain the prophetic proof that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
Full insertion of the glans, even without ejaculation, makes ghusl obligatory.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling of janabah: what exactly makes ghusl obligatory after sexual intercourse? The Hanafi school, supported by explicit hadith, holds that the mere act of insertion – the disappearance of the glans – is the cause, irrespective of seminal discharge. We will analyse the key terms, the prophetic text, and the school's reasoning, including the boundary cases that confirm the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the central claim: ghusl is wajib (fard 'ayn) upon the active and passive participants due to 'ghaybat al-hashafah' in the front or back. Note that the term 'ghusl' here refers to the full ritual bath for janabah.
The passage uses 'ghaybat' (disappearance), not mere contact.
2
Locate the dalil and its authority
Find the hadith cited: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether one ejaculates or not.' Identify its narrators (al-Tabarani, Bukhari, Muslim). Note that the hadith is ahad in transmission but its meaning is clear and accepted.
The school relies on the linguistic clarity of the condition 'ghābat al-hashafah'.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith directly proves the ruling. The conditional statement 'idhā... wajaba' indicates causality: the disappearance of the glans is the sole trigger. The appended phrase 'anzala aw lam yunzil' explicitly negates any condition of ejaculation.
The Hanafi principle 'al-amru yafīdu al-wujūb' is applied to the imperative 'wajaba'.
4
Examine the edge cases (mawani')
Review the boundary cases that confirm the rule by exception: insertion of a finger or an animal's penis does not cause ghusl; however, intercourse with a jinn does. These rulings reinforce that the cause is specifically the human glans.
The term 'hashafah' is defined as the glans of a human (or jinn), excluding other objects.
5
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
Recognize that some Shafi'i scholars require ejaculation for ghusl. The Hanafi position is based on the literal text; the disagreement is legitimate but the Hanafi view is the mufta bihi.
The practical difference: in Hanafi fiqh, a person who engages in intercourse without ejaculation must still perform ghusl before prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغيبةُ حَشَفةٍ في قبل أو دُبُرٍ على الفاعل والمفعول به

قوله : وغيبة ... الخ ؛ الغَيبة - بالفتح – مصدر غاب الشيء إذا استتر
والحشفة بفتحات رأس الذكر إلى المقطع
والقبل : بالضم وسكون الباء وبضمتين : فرج المرأة.
والدبر : بالضم وبضمتين.
وفيه إشارة إلى أن موجب الغسل نفس الإدخال، وإن لم ينزل الحديث : «إذا التقى الختانان وغابت الحشفة، وجب الغسل أنزلَ أو لم ينزل»)، أخرجه الطبراني

الفرج لا يجب عليها الغُسل كما في «الخلاصة».
(۱) خلاصة الفتاوى (۱ : ۱۳).

«التجنيس والمزيد».
ثم المراد بالحشفة حشفة الآدمي أو الجني، فلو ولج ذكر البهائم في فرجها لا غسل
عليها ما لم تنزل، صرح به في «البناية». ولو وطئها جني وجب عليها الغُسل ، صرّح به في آكام المرجان في أحكام
الجان».
And the disappearance of the glans (hashafah) in the front (qabl) or back (dubur) necessitates ghusl upon the active and passive participants. His saying: 'and ghaybah... etc.' – al-ghaybah with fatha is the masdar of ghāba al-shay' (the thing disappeared). al-hashafah with three fatahat is the head of the penis up to the point of circumcision. al-qabl with dammah and sukun of the ba' or with two dammahs: the vulva of a woman. al-dubur with dammah or two dammahs. In it is an indication that the cause of ghusl is the insertion itself, even if no seminal discharge occurs, due to the hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether one ejaculates or not.' Narrated by al-Tabarani and others, and similarly in Sahih al-Bukhari, Muslim, and the Sunan. And an indication that if one has intercourse without the glans disappearing but semen exits and flows into the vulva, ghusl is not obligatory upon her, as in al-Khulāsa. ... And an indication that if one inserts a finger or similar into the front or back, no ghusl is required, as in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. Then by hashafah is meant the hashafah of a human or a jinn. So if the penis of an animal enters her vulva, no ghusl is required of her unless she experiences orgasm, as stated in al-Bināya. And if a jinn has intercourse with her, ghusl becomes obligatory upon her, as stated in Ākām al-Marjān fī Ahkām al-Jān.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the obligation of ghusl (ritual bath) due to sexual intercourse. It begins by defining key terms: 'ghaybat al-hashafah' (disappearance of the glans), 'qabl' (vagina), and 'dubur' (anus). The matn asserts that this act necessitates ghusl for both the active and passive participants. The commentator expands by citing the well-known hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether one ejaculates or not' (narrated by al-Tabarani, Bukhari, Muslim). This establishes that the mere act of insertion, irrespective of emission, triggers janābah. The text also addresses edge cases: if intercourse occurs without full insertion but semen is discharged into the vulva, ghusl is not required (as per al-Khulāsa). Similarly, inserting a finger or similar object does not necessitate ghusl. The discussion concludes with rulings concerning non-human entities: if an animal's penis enters a woman's vulva, no ghusl is required unless she has an orgasm; however, if a jinn has intercourse with her, ghusl is obligatory. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle that the cause of ghusl is the insertion of the human glans, not mere contact or emission.

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafah): The head of the penis up to the point of circumcision.
قبل (qabl): The vulva (female genitalia).
دبر (dubur): The anus.
غسل (ghusl): The full-body ritual bath that becomes obligatory upon janabah due to intercourse or seminal emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full insertion of the glans into the vagina, even if no ejaculation occurs.
B) Insertion of a finger into the vagina with seminal emission.
C) External ejaculation near the vulva without any insertion.
D) Full insertion of an animal's penis into a woman's vulva.

Key Takeaway
The sole cause of ghusl from intercourse is the full disappearance of the glans into the vagina or anus, regardless of ejaculation.

Ghusl for Wetness Found Upon Waking: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on ghusl for wetness upon waking, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl when waking with wetness, identify the positions of Abu Yusuf versus the two imams, and apply the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) to a doubtful case.

Core Idea
When in doubt, the wetness is treated as semen; ghusl is required even without a dream.

It is a common occurrence to wake up and find a damp spot without remembering a dream. While the ruling for clear semen is obvious, uncertainty raises a question: is ghusl needed? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point, but the later relied-upon position requires ghusl. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical evidence
You find wetness on your bed or thigh. Determine the type: manī (semen), madhi (pre-ejaculate), or wady (prostatic). Recollection of a wet dream is a factor.
2
Apply the default presumption (istishāb)
In the absence of certainty, Hanafis presume the fluid is manī until proven otherwise, because madhi can be thinned semen.
This is a key usul principle.
3
Distinguish between Abu Yusuf and the two imams
Abu Yusuf requires subjective certainty (dream recollection) to confirm manī; the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely solely on the physical sign.
Both are valid Hanafi positions.
4
Trace the evidential basis
The two imams reason that the possibility of the fluid being manī is enough to trigger ghusl; Abu Yusuf demands additional circumstantial evidence (dream).
The dalil is qiyas on the known case of clear manī.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its consequence
The view of the two is operative in fatwa; therefore, any plausible wetness triggers ghusl.
This is the precautionary position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورؤية المستيقظ المني، أو المذي وإن لم يحتلم). أما في المني فظاهر، وأما في المذي" ؛ فلاحتمال كونه منيّاً رَقَ بحرارة البدن ، وفيه خلاف لأبي يوسف .

[٢]قوله : وأما في المذي ؛ قال في «الذخيرة» : إذا استيقظ ووجد على فراشه أو فخذه بلة، وهو يتذكر احتلاماً إن تيقن أنه مني أو تيقن أنه مذي ، أو شك أنه مني أو مذي فعليه الغسل، وإن تيقن أنه ودي لا غُسلَ عليه ، وإن لم يتذكر الاحتلام إن تيقن آنه وديّ لا غسل عليه، وان تيقن أنه مني كان عليه الغسل، وإن تيقن أنه مني أو مذي، قال أبو يوسف : لا يجب الغُسلُ حتى يتيقن بالاحتلام، وقالا : يجب الغسل.
And [a cause of ghusl is] a waking person seeing semen (manī) or pre-seminal fluid (madhi) even if he did not have a wet dream. As for semen, it is apparent [that ghusl is required]; as for pre-seminal fluid, due to the possibility that it is semen thinned by the body's heat, and concerning this, there is a disagreement from Abu Yusuf. His saying: 'As for madhi'; it is said in al-Dhakhira: If one wakes up and finds wetness on his bed or thigh, and he recalls having a wet dream: if he is certain it is semen or certain it is madhi, or doubts whether it is semen or madhi, then ghusl is obligatory upon him; if he is certain it is wady (prostatic fluid), no ghusl is required. And if he does not recall a wet dream: if he is certain it is wady, no ghusl; if he is certain it is semen, ghusl is required; if he is certain it is semen or madhi, Abu Yusuf said: ghusl is not obligatory until he is certain of a wet dream, while the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said: ghusl is obligatory.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation of ghusl upon waking up to find wetness on oneself or one's clothing. The matn states that ghusl is necessary if one sees manī (semen) or madhi (pre-ejaculatory fluid), even without recollection of a wet dream. The commentator clarifies: for manī, the ruling is obvious due to its known property. For madhi, it is included because it may be thinned semen due to body heat, so it is treated as semen until proven otherwise. An intra-Hanafi dispute is then detailed: Abu Yusuf holds that if a person finds wetness but does not recall a wet dream, and is uncertain whether it is manī or madhi, ghusl is not obligatory until he is certain of having had a wet dream. However, Imām Abū Hanīfa and Imām Muhammad (the two) hold that ghusl is obligatory in such uncertainty because the default is that wetness is considered manī unless proven otherwise. The relied-upon position (muftā bihi) is that of the two, requiring ghusl in cases of doubt. This disagreement stems from differing views on the evidentiary weight of contextual clues versus the external appearance of the fluid.

Key Terms
مني (manī): Semen, the reproductive fluid whose emergence (whether in dream or wakefulness) necessitates ghusl.
مذي (madhi): Pre-ejaculatory fluid; in the context of waking up, it is considered presumptively manī thinned by heat.
احتلام (ihtilām): A wet dream; recollection of a wet dream is a factor in Abu Yusuf's view for certainty, but not required by the two.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in this passage, what is required when a person wakes up and finds wetness but does not recall a wet dream?
A) No ghusl is required until certainty of a wet dream
B) Ghusl is required if the wetness could be manī or madhi
C) Only wudu is required
D) Ghusl is required only if the wetness is clearly manī

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the default presumption when finding wetness upon waking without a dream is that it is semen, thus necessitating ghusl.

Ghusl After Menstruation and Postpartum Bleeding: The Cause and Proof
Ruling on ghusl after haid and nifas, with Quranic proof and commentary refinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when ghusl becomes obligatory after haid/nifas, identify the Quranic proof, and explain the commentator's refinement regarding the cause.

Core Idea
Cessation of bleeding is the sign; the blood itself invalidates purity and necessitates future ghusl.

The obligation of ghusl after menstruation and postpartum bleeding seems straightforward, but a refined understanding of its cause is important. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, its Quranic evidence, and a subtle clarification from the commentary that distinguishes between the invalidating event (blood exit) and the triggering condition (cessation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on the obligation (fard) of ghusl when menstrual or postpartum bleeding ceases completely. The act is ghusl, and the hukm is fard 'ayn.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quranic: 'Do not approach them until they become pure' (2:222) with the reading with tashdid, indicating purification by ghusl.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of intercourse continues 'until they become pure', which the majority interpret as performing ghusl after bleeding stops. The word 'yaṭhurna' (with tashdid) explicitly connects to purification via ghusl.
4
Analyse the commentator's objection
The commentator notes that if cessation were the cause, it would imply that before cessation the woman remains pure, which is false. He refines: the exit of blood is what invalidates purity, and cessation merely signals the obligation of ghusl.
5
Accept the refined phrasing
The correct causative chain: the exit of blood invalidates past purity, and the cessation of bleeding makes ghusl necessary for future purity. Thus the ruling stands: ghusl is obligatory when bleeding stops.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانقطاع الحيض والنفاس (۳) ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا نَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ ﴾ على قراءة التشديد، ولما كان الانقطاع سبباً للغُسل ، فإذا انقطع

[٣]قوله : وانقطاع الحيض والنفاس ؛ فيه أنّ الانقطاع طهارة، فكيف يكون موجباً للطهارة، وأيضاً لو كان الانقطاع موجباً لزم أن تكون الحائض والنفساء قبل الانقطاع محكوماً عليها ببقاء الطهارة، وليس كذلك، فالأولى أن يقال: خروج دم الحيض والنفاس، فإنّه الناقض الطهارة في الماضي، وموجب لطهارة في الزمان الآتي.
[٤] قوله : لقوله تعالى : حاصله : أن الله قال: ﴿ وَيَسْتَلُونَك يا محمد عَنِ الْمَحِيضِ : أي دم الحيض قُل في جوابهم : هُوَ أَذًى ) : أي نجاسة
And [a cause of ghusl is] the cessation of menstruation (haid) and postpartum bleeding (nifas); due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And do not approach them until they become pure' according to the reading with tashdid (emphasis), and since cessation is a cause for ghusl, so when it ceases ... His saying: 'And cessation of menstruation and postpartum bleeding'; in it [there is an objection] that cessation is itself purity, so how can it be the cause of purity? Also, if cessation were the cause, then the menstruating woman and postpartum woman before cessation would be ruled as remaining in a state of purity, which is not the case. So it is better to say: the exit of menstrual and postpartum blood, for it is what invalidates purity in the past and necessitates purity in the future. His saying: 'due to His statement, the Exalted': its gist is that Allah said: 'And they ask you, O Muhammad, about menstruation: say: it is harm (i.e., impurity).'
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage establishes the cessation of menstrual (haid) and postpartum (nifas) bleeding as a cause for ghusl. The proof is the Quranic verse: 'Do not approach them until they become pure' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:222) read with tashdid (yat̤h̤urna), which implies purification through ghusl. The commentator addresses a subtle objection: cessation is itself a state of purity, so how can it be the cause of purity? The objection notes that if cessation alone caused ghusl, then before cessation the woman would still be considered pure (since the invalidator is blood, not cessation). The commentator resolves this by stating that it is more accurate to say that the occurrence (khurūj) of menstrual or postpartum blood invalidates purity at the time of exit and necessitates future purity (i.e., ghusl upon cessation). That is, the blood is the invalidator, and its end (cessation) triggers the obligation to perform ghusl. The Hanafi position is that when bleeding stops completely, ghusl becomes wajib (obligatory) before resuming prayer, fasting, etc.

Key Terms
حيض (haid): Menstrual blood; its end necessitates ghusl.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding; its end similarly necessitates ghusl.
انقطاع (inqitā'): Cessation; the end of bleeding, which triggers the obligation of ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which of the following best describes the cause of ghusl after menstruation?
A) The cessation of blood itself is the cause of ghusl.
B) The exit of blood invalidates past purity and cessation necessitates future ghusl.
C) The presence of blood directly triggers the obligation of ghusl.
D) The duration of bleeding determines when ghusl becomes fard.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl after haid/nifas is fard 'ayn upon complete cessation; the exit of blood invalidates purity, and cessation signals the obligation.

Causes of Ghusl: Emission and Cessation
Expansion on causes of ghusl with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two primary causes of ghusl in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement regarding madhi found upon waking.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib upon seeing maniy/madhi after sleep and upon cessation of hayd/nifas — the proof and dispute reveal Hanafi methodology.

This lesson examines the causes that make ritual bath (ghusl) obligatory. The Hanafi school identifies two primary causes: the emission of semen or pre-ejaculate fluid (maniy/madhi) upon waking and the cessation of menstrual or postpartum bleeding. The discussion also clarifies the intra-Hanafi disagreement over madhi found without a wet dream, and the Quranic proof from Surah al-Baqarah. By the end, you will be able to articulate the rulings and the evidence behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes
Read the passage to find the two main scenarios that obligate ghusl: (1) seeing maniy or madhi upon waking, even without a wet dream; (2) cessation of hayd (menstruation) or nifas (postpartum bleeding).
2
Understand the reasoning for madhi
The author explains that madhi is treated like maniy because it might be thin semen due to body heat. This is the basis for the majority ruling.
Contrast with the Shafi'i view that madhi only requires wudu.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that finding madhi without a wet dream does not obligate ghusl unless the wet dream is certain. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) hold that ghusl is obligatory regardless.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse (2:222) with the qira'ah of tashdid (yatṭahharna) is cited. The reading meaning 'until they bathe' indicates that intercourse is prohibited before ghusl, proving its obligation.
The alternative reading without tashdid only indicates cessation of blood, not ghusl.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a waking person finds wetness from maniy or madhi (or uncertainty), the Hanafi ruling is that ghusl is wajib. For cessation of hayd/nifas, ghusl is also wajib.
Secondary rulings about insertion and animal/jinn intercourse are further applications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة/ الغُسل
ورؤية المستيقظ المني، أو المذي وإن لم يحتلم)؛ أما في المني فظاهر، وأما في المذي؛ فلاحتمال كونه منيّاً رَقَ بحرارة البدن، وفيه خلاف لأبي يوسف. وانقطاع الحيض والنفاس؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ ﴾ على قراءة التشديد، ولما كان الانقطاع سبباً للغُسل، فإذا انقطع وإلى أنه لو أدخل الأصبع ونحوها في القبل أو الدبر لا غسل عليه كما في «التجنيس والمزيد».
ثم المراد بالحشفة حشفة الآدمي أو الجني، فلو ولج ذكر البهائم في فرجها لا غسل عليها ما لم تنزل، صرح به في «البناية». ولو وطئها جني وجب عليها الغُسل، صرّح به في «آكام المرجان في أحكام الجان».
[١]قوله: ورؤية المستيقظ ... الخ؛ هذا التطويلُ بلا فائدة، ولو زاد بعد قوله: ولو في نوم، ولو كان الخارج مذياً لكفى.
[٢]قوله: وأما في المذي؛ قال في «الذخيرة»: إذا استيقظ ووجد على فراشه أو فخذه بلة، وهو يتذكر احتلاماً إن تيقن أنه مني أو تيقن أنه مذي، أو شك أنه مني أو مذي فعليه الغسل، وإن تيقن أنه ودي لا غُسلَ عليه، وإن لم يتذكر الاحتلام إن تيقن أنه ودي لا غسل عليه، وإن تيقن أنه مني كان عليه الغسل، وإن تيقن أنه مني أو مذي، قال أبو يوسف: لا يجب الغُسلُ حتى يتيقن بالاحتلام، وقالا: يجب الغسل.
[٣]قوله: وانقطاع الحيض والنفاس؛ فيه أنّ الانقطاع طهارة، فكيف يكون موجباً للطهارة، وأيضاً لو كان الانقطاع موجباً لزم أن تكون الحائض والنفساء قبل الانقطاع محكوماً عليها ببقاء الطهارة، وليس كذلك، فالأولى أن يقال: خروج دم الحيض والنفاس، فإنّه الناقض الطهارة في الماضي، وموجب لطهارة في الزمان الآتي.
[٤] قوله: لقوله تعالى: حاصله: أن الله قال: ﴿ وَيَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْمَحِيضِ قُلْ هُوَ أَذًى ﴾، ثم أسلمت لا يلزمها الاغتسال؛ إذ وقت الانقطاع كانت كافرة، وهي غير مأمورة بالشرائع عندنا، ومتى أسلمت لم يوجد السبب، وهو الانقطاع، بخلاف ما إذا أجنبت الكافرة، ثم أسلمت، حيث يجب عليها غُسل الجنابة؛ لأنَّ الجنابة أمر مستمر، فتكون جنباً بعد الإسلام.
فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ، قُرى بتشديد الطاء والهاء فمعناه: حتى يغتسلن، وقرئ بسكون الطاء وضم الهاء مخففاً فمعناه: حتى ينقطع دم حيضهن، كذا ذكره المفسرون، فهذه الآية دلت على حرمة الوطء قبل الاغتسال. ومن المعلوم أن الوطء تصرف واقع في ملكه، فلو كان الاغتسال جائزاً ومستحباً لم يمنع الزوج من الوطء، فعلم أنه واجب، وبهذا ظهر وجه اختيار قراءة التشديد، فإنّه على قراءة التخفيف يكون مفسّراً بانقطاع الدم، فلا يدل على وجوب الغسل. فإن قلت: فأين ذكر النفاس. قلت: فهم من هذه الآية ضمناً بقوله: هُوَ أذى، فإن دم الحيض والنفاس مشتركاً في كونه أذى.
[1] قوله: عندنا؛ ظاهره أنه متفق عليه بين أصحابنا، وليس كذلك، قال ابن الهمام في «تحرير الأصول»: «عدم كون الكفار مكلفين بالفروع مذهب مشايخ سمرقند، ومن عداهم متَّفقون على التكليف بها، وإنّما اختلفوا في أنه في حق الاعتقاد فقط، أو الاعتقاد والعمل كليهما، فقال البخاريون بالأوّل، فعندهم يعاقب الكفار على ترك الاعتقاد بها، وعلى ترك الاعتقادِ بالإيمان وتركه، وقال العراقيون بالثاني كالشافعية».
(۱) البقرة: من الآية ۲۲۲
(۲) اختلفوا في تخفيف الطاء وضم الهاء وتشديد الطاء وفتح الهاء من قوله: حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ فقرأ ابن كثير، ونافع، وأبو عمرو، وابن عامر: يَطْهُرْنَ خفيفة. وقرأ عاصم في رواية أبي بكر، والمفضل وحمزة، والكسائي: يَطْهُرْنَ مشددة. وقرأ حفص عن عاصم: يَطْهُرْنَ خفيفة. ينظر: «السبعة في القراءات»(۱ : ۱۸۲)، و«حجة القراءات»(۱ : ١٣٥).
Book of purification / Ghusl. And [the cause includes] the waking person seeing maniy or madhi even if he did not have a wet dream; as for maniy it is apparent, and as for madhi because of the possibility that it is maniy that became thin due to body heat, and there is a disagreement regarding it from Abu Yusuf. And [the cause includes] the cessation of menstrual and postpartum bleeding; due to His statement, the Exalted: "And do not approach them until they become pure" according to the reading with tashdid, and since cessation is a cause for ghusl, so when it ceases... And that if one inserts a finger or similar into the front or back, there is no ghusl upon him, as in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. Then, the meaning of 'hashafah' is the glans of a human or a jinn; so if the penis of an animal enters her private part, there is no ghusl upon her unless she has an orgasm, as stated in al-Bināyah. And if a jinn has intercourse with her, ghusl becomes obligatory upon her, as stated in Ākām al-Marjān fī Ahkām al-Jān. [1] His statement: "and the waking person seeing" etc.; this lengthening is without benefit, and had he added after his statement: "even if in sleep", and if the emission was madhi, it would have sufficed. [2] His statement: "and as for madhi"; it is said in al-Dhakhīrah: if one wakes up and finds wetness on his bed or thigh, and he remembers a wet dream, if he is certain it is maniy or certain it is madhi, or doubts whether it is maniy or madhi, then ghusl is upon him. And if he is certain it is wady, no ghusl upon him. And if he does not remember a wet dream: if he is certain it is wady, no ghusl; if he is certain it is maniy, ghusl is upon him; and if he is certain it is maniy or madhi, Abu Yusuf said: ghusl is not obligatory until he is certain of the wet dream, and the two said: ghusl is obligatory. [3] His statement: "and the cessation of menstrual and postpartum bleeding"; in it [there is an issue]: that cessation is purity, so how can it be a cause for purity? Also, if cessation were a cause, it would necessitate that the menstruating and postpartum woman before cessation be considered as remaining in a state of purity, which is not the case. So it is better to say: the emergence of menstrual and postpartum blood, for it is what nullifies purity in the past and causes purity in the future. [4] His statement: "due to His statement"; its summary: that Allah said: "And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm." Then she [a woman] converted to Islam, ghusl is not incumbent on her; because at the time of cessation she was a disbeliever, and she is not commanded with the religious laws according to us, and when she converted the cause [cessation] no longer existed. Unlike the case when a disbelieving woman becomes junub, then converts, where ghusl is obligatory upon her; because janābah is a continuous matter, so she is junub after Islam. "So keep away from women during menstruation, and do not approach them until they become pure." It was recited with tashdid of the ta and ha, meaning: until they perform ghusl; and it was recited with sukun of the ta and dammah of the ha lightly, meaning: until their menstrual blood ceases, as the commentators mentioned. This verse indicates the prohibition of intercourse before ghusl. And it is known that intercourse is an action occurring within his ownership; if ghusl were merely permissible or recommended, it would not prevent the husband from intercourse. So it is known that it is obligatory. And by this the reason for preferring the reading with tashdid becomes apparent; for according to the light reading, it is interpreted as cessation of blood, so it does not indicate the obligation of ghusl. If you say: So where is the mention of postpartum bleeding? I say: It is understood from this verse implicitly by His statement: "It is harm", for menstrual blood and postpartum blood share in being harm. [1] His statement: "according to us"; apparently it is agreed upon among our companions, but it is not so. Ibn al-Humām said in Tahrīr al-Uṣūl: "The position that disbelievers are not obligated with the branches [of the law] is the madhhab of the scholars of Samarqand, while others agree that they are obligated with them. They only differed whether it is in respect of belief only, or both belief and action. The Bukhārīs held the first, so according to them disbelievers are punished for abandoning belief in them and for abandoning belief in faith and abandoning it; the Iraqīs held the second, like the Shāfi'īs." (1) al-Baqarah: part of verse 222. (2) They differed on the lightening of the ta and dammah of the ha and the tashdid of the ta and fath of the ha from His statement "until they become pure". Ibn Kathīr, Nāfi', Abū 'Amr, and Ibn 'Āmir read: yaṭhurna lightly. 'Āṣim in the narration of Abū Bakr, al-Mufaḍḍal, Ḥamzah, and al-Kisā'ī read: yaṭṭahharna with tashdid. Ḥafṣ from 'Āṣim read: yaṭhurna lightly. See: al-Sab'ah fī al-Qirā'āt (1:182) and Ḥujjat al-Qirā'āt (1:135).
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the causes that make ritual bath (ghusl) obligatory. The author identifies two primary causes: (1) upon waking, seeing either semen (maniy) or pre-ejaculate fluid (madhi) on one's person or clothing, even without recollection of a wet dream; (2) the cessation of menstrual bleeding (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas). The reasoning for madhi is that it might be thin semen due to body heat. A difference from Abu Yusuf is noted: he requires certainty of a wet dream for madhi to necessitate ghusl, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) hold that ghusl is obligatory regardless of recollection. The proof for cessation is the Quranic verse (2:222) in the reading with tashdid (yatṭahharna), which means 'until they bathe', indicating the obligation of ghusl. The author also addresses minutiae: inserting a finger into the front or back does not require ghusl; the glans in question is that of a human or jinn, not an animal; intercourse with an animal does not obligate ghusl unless emission occurs; intercourse with a jinn does obligate ghusl. The commentary then clarifies the reasoning for cessation being a cause, resolving that it is actually the end of the blood that constitutes purity, not the cessation per se. The discussion concludes with a digression on whether disbelievers are obligated with the branches of law, noting a difference between the scholars of Samarqand and others.

Key Terms
المذي (al-madhyu): Pre-ejaculate fluid that is emitted during foreplay or arousal, not necessarily accompanied by orgasm. In this context, it is considered a potential cause for ghusl if found upon waking.
المني (al-maniyyu): Semen, the fluid emitted at orgasm. Its sight upon waking necessitates ghusl by consensus.
الحشفة (al-hashafah): The glans of the penis. The text specifies that for ghusl to be obligatory due to insertion, the glans must be that of a human or jinn, not an animal.
الجني (al-jinniyyu): A jinn (spirit being). The text rules that intercourse with a jinn obligates ghusl on the woman, treating the jinn's copulation like that of a human.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence cited in the passage for the obligation of ghusl after menstruation?
A) Surah al-Baqarah 2:222 read with tashdid (yatṭahharna)
B) Surah al-Nisa 4:43
C) Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6
D) Surah al-Nur 24:31

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes obligatory (wajib) upon seeing maniy or madhi after sleep, and upon the end of menstruation or postpartum bleeding.
